Jamison Brereton

66 (507)
Maruts
Bharadv─Бja B─Бrhaspatya
11 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
The only hymn to the Maruts in Maс╣Зс╕Нala VI, this poem is complex, playful, allu sive, and very difficult in parts.
It begins with five dense and syntactically contorted verses about the birth of the Maruts, a topic that regularly invites such treatment. The story of the birth is introduced by a signal that it is esoteric knowledge; verse 1a announces it as a mar vel even for someone who really perceives properly. The rest of the verse is both a paradox and a riddle: two entities have the same name, тАЬmilker,тАЭ but one of them constantly gives milk, and the other has done so only once. The riddle is solved by the last word of the verse, тАЬudderтАЭ; the paradox juxtaposes the normal udder of a cow, which constantly swells with milk, with the udder of the MarutтАЩs mother, Pr╠е┼Ыni, who bore them, that is, milked them out, all at once. (This same phenom
enon is referred to in riddling terms in VI.48.22.) Verse 2 continues this theme, and the other parent of the Maruts, their father Rudra, is introduced in verse 3. But both 1 and 3 also allude to the androgynous behavior of the mother Pr╠е┼Ыni, who elsewhere (see esp. IV.3.10) is identified as a bull who gives milk that is identical with semen; in verse 3 here she is the subject of the quintessentially male verb of impregnation (ga╠Бrbhaс╣Г тИЪdh─Б тАЬimplant an embryoтАЭ). Verse 4 is the most opaque verse in this sequence. It clearly describes the moment of the MarutsтАЩ birth; they did not resist being born, but in fact were milked out when they wished, after hav ing тАЬpurified their flawsтАЭ while still within her womb. A two-word expression early in the verse (a╠Бy─Б n├║) seems to have a double meaning: on the one hand, it is the poetтАЩs comment about the manner of birth: тАЬnow (it happened) in this wayтАЭ; on the other, it can be read as the direct speech of the Maruts (considered as a group), тАЬNow I will goтАЭ (that is, be born), an indication of their moment of choice. The final verse of the birth story relates the fact that Pr╠е┼Ыni, having given them as milk, did not give them milk after they were born, but they were undeterred. There is much that is doubtful in our translation of these verses, but the main outlines seem clear, while the tricks of the poet are much on display.
Though more of his tricks appear in the rest of the hymn, none of it is as dif ficult as these first five verses. Verse 6 turns on a pun between the word for the тАЬtwo world-halvesтАЭ (ro╠Бdas─л) and the female who is often found as the MarutsтАЩ lover, Rodas─л╠Б (distinguished from the first only by accent). The marvel of their journey through the midspace is described in verse 7, and the good fortune of the man who receives their aid in verse 8. The journey of verse 7 must be to carry them to our sac rifice, for the remaining verses bring the hymn to a fairly conventional end: in verse 9 we produce a hymn for the Maruts; in verse 10 they are compared to the ritual fire, an appropriate simile if they are situated on the ritual ground; in the final verse (10) the aim of attracting them to the sacrifice is made explicit and the competing hymns of rival sacrificers are alluded to.
Unlike many Marut hymns, this one lacks any significant description of their thunderstorm-like aspects.

рддрддреН рдкреНрд░рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрдВ рд╕рдорд╛рдирдореН рдПрдХрд░реВрдкрдореН ред рдорд░реБрддрдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рджрд╛ рд╕рдорд╛рдирд░реВрдкрд╛рдГ ред рддрдерд╛ рдЪ рдирд┐рдЧрдорд╛рдиреНрддрд░рдореН – тАШ рдЕрдЬреНрдпреЗрд╖реНрдард╛рд╕реЛ рдЕрдХрдирд┐рд╖реНрдард╛рд╕ рдПрддреЗ ’ ( рдЛ. рд╕рдВ. рел.ремреж.рел ) рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдирд╛рдо рд╕реНрдерд┐рд░рд╛рдгрд╛рдордкрд┐ рдирд╛рдордХрдВ рдзреЗрдиреБ рдкреНрд░реАрдгрдпрд┐рддреГ рдкрддреНрдпрдорд╛рдирдВ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рджрд╛ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддреН рд╡рдкреБрдГ рдорд░реБрддрд╛рдВ рд░реВрдкрдВ рдЪрд┐рдХрд┐рддреБрд╖реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреБрд╖реЗ рд╕реНрддреЛрддреНрд░реЗ рдиреБ рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкреНрд░рдореН рдЕрд╕реНрддреБ рдкреНрд░рд╛рджреБрд░реНрднрд╡рддреБред рдЪрд┐рддреН рдЗрддрд┐ рдкреВрд░рдХрдореН ред рдХрд┐рдВрдЪ рддрджреНрд░реВрдкрдВ рдорд░реНрддреЗрд╖реБ рдорд░реНрддреНрдпрд▓реЛрдХреЗ рдЕрдиреНрдпрддреН рдУрд╖рдзрд┐рд╡рдирд╕реНрдкрддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рдХрдВ рджреЛрд╣рд╕реЗ рдХрд╛рдорд╛рдиреН рджреЛрдЧреНрдзреБрдВ рдкреАрдкрд╛рдп рдЖрдкреНрдпрд╛рдпрдпрддрд┐ ред рдХрд┐рдВрдЪ рдорд░реБрддрд╛рдореЗрд╡ рдирд┐рд░реНрджреЗрд╢рд╛рддреН рдкреГрд╢реНрдирд┐рдГ рдЕрдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖рдВ рд╕рдХреГрддреН рд╕рдВрд╡рддреНрд╕рд░рд╕реНрдп рд╡рд░реНрд╖рд╛рд╕реБ рд╢реБрдХреНрд░рдВ рд╢реБрдХреНрд▓рд╡рд░реНрдгрдореН рдКрдзрдГ рдЙрджрдХрдВ рджреБрджреБрд╣реЗ рдХреНрд╖рд░рддрд┐ рее

English translation:

тАЬMay the like-formed, benevolent, all-pervading, all humiliating troop (of the Maruts) be promptly with the prudent man; the troop that ever cherishes all that among mortals is designed to yield (them) advantage; and (at whose wil) Pс╣Ы┼Ыni gives milk from (her) bright udder once (in the year).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

That ever cherishes: martteс╣гu anyad dohase p─лp─Бya = tad r┼лpam (marut─Бm), martyaloke anyad oс╣гadhi vanaspaty─Бdikam k─Бm─Бn dogdhum ─Бy─Бyagoti, that form of the Maruts cause one or other thing in the world, herbaceous plural nts, forest trees, and the like, of flourish, so as to milk or yield wht is desired;

Pс╣Ы┼Ыni: implies the firmament, which, by the influence of the winds, sends down its milk, i.e. rain, once, i.e. at the rainy season

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬUnsoiled by dust the golden chariots of those Maruts, who are shining like kindled fires, enlarging themselves (at will) twofold and threefold, and (charged) with riches and virile energies, are manifest.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Those who kept blazing up like fires being kindled, when the Maruts were strengthened two or three times overтАФ
dustless, golden were their (chariots)тАФthey came into being all at once with their manly and male powers.

Griffith

They who like kindled flames of fire are glowing,. the Maruts, twice and thrice have waxen mighty.
Golden and dustless were their cars, invested with their great strength and their heroic vigour.

Geldner

Die gleich entbrannten Feuern ergl├╝hten, als die Marut zweimal und dreimal st├дrker wurden - ihre staublosen goldigen Wagen sind zugleich mit ihren Manneskr├дften und St├дrken entstanden.

Grassmann

Sie, die erstrahlten wie entflammte Feuer, die Maruts, als sie zwiefach, dreifach wuchsen; Staublos, mit Gold bedeckt sind ihre Leiber, begabt mit Mannes- und mit Heldenkr├дften;

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬThey who approach not to men any conveyance, being already in their hearts, purifying their defects; when brilliant they supply their milk (the rain) for the gratification (of their worshippers); they are watering the earth (manifesting their collective); from with splendour.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Being already in their hearts: the Maruts are regarded as identical wit the Pr─Бс╣З─Бс╕е, vital airs

Jamison Brereton

Those who do not retreat from their birth: now (it happened) in this way [/(saying) тАЬNow I will goтАЭ]тАФpurifying their flaws while still within
(their mother),
they were milked forth gleaming, at their pleasure, growing in splendor all along their bodies.

Griffith

They shrink not from the birth; in this same manner still resting there they purge away reproaches.
When they have streamed forth, brilliant, at their pleasure, with their own splendour they bedew their bodies.

Geldner

Die nicht vor der Geburt auf diese Art zur├╝ckscheuen, noch im Inneren der Mutter sich von jedem Makel reinigend, da sie blank nach ihrem Belieben ausgemolken werden, indem sie mit ihrem Leib entsprechend wachsen.

Grassmann

Die nicht verleugnen die Geburt aus jener, im Mutterleib schon tilgend ihre Flecken; Sobald die reinen nach Gefallen sogen, betr├дufelten mit Glanz sie ihre Leiber.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬApproaching nigh to whom, and repeating the mighty name of the Maruts, (the worshipper is able) quickly to obtain (his wishes); the liberal donor pacifies the angry Maruts, who are otherwise in their might the resistless plural nderers (of their wealth).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

He pacifies those na ye staun─Б ay─Бso mahn─Б nu cid, who now are thieves going with greatness verily ever

Jamison Brereton

Those for whom even right away [=right after their birth] the irrepressible one [=Pr╠е┼Ыni] was not there to give milkтАФthose who, assuming the bold name тАЬMarut,тАЭ
did not (stand still) like posts, (but were themselves) irrepressible in their greatness. Even now [/never] would the one of good drops [=Pr╠е┼Ыni]
appease (those) mighty ones.

Griffith

Even those who bear the brave bold name of Maruts, whom not the active quickly wins for milking.
Even the liberal wards not off those fierce ones, those who are light and agile in their greatness.

Geldner

Alsbald nehmen sie, bei denen die Unerschrockene nicht erst zu melken war, ihren k├╝hnen marutischen Namen an, die nicht ohne Lob die Unerschrockenen sind infolge ihrer Gr├╢├Яe. Niemals soll die gabensch├╢ne Mutter den Gewaltigen Abbitte tun.

Grassmann

Sobald aus ihr nichts blieb f├╝r sie zu saugen, erlangten sie den k├╝hnen Marutnamen, Die nimmer rasten, munter eilend, herrlich, nie weis’ die starken ab der opferreiche.

Elizarenkova

рдорд╛рдирд╕рддрд░рдЩреНрдЧрд┐рдгреАрдХреГрддреН

Indeed, these fierce ones, with might, formidably armed,
they have yoked the two well-formed hemispheres of the universe.
further, the self-radiant rodasI appeared among them,
standing among the impetuous ones, like a source of light.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬTHose fierce and powerfully arrayed (Maruts) unite by their strength the two beautiful (regions) heaven and earth; in them, the self-radiant, heaven and earth abide; the obstruction (of light) dwells not in those mighty ones.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Unite by their strength: by the rain, which may be said to form a bond of union between heaven and earth

Jamison Brereton

Just these mighty ones in a bold host yoked both well-fixed
world-halves [=r├│das─л] through their vast power.
Then Rodas─л mounted among these impetuous ones like a
self-blazing light.

Griffith

When, strong in strength and armed with potent weapons, they had united wellformed earth and heaven,
Rodasl stood among these furious Heroes like splendour shining with her native brightness.

Geldner

Diese an Macht Gewaltigen, die eine k├╝hne Heerschar bilden, spannten sich die festgegr├╝ndeten Welth├дlften vor. Dann ist zu ihnen, den Wuchtigen, die von selbst flammende Rodasi wie eine Leuchte auf den Wagen aufgestiegen.

Grassmann

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay your chariot, Maruts, be devoid of wickedness; that which (the worshipper) impels, and which without driver, without horses, without provender, without traces, scattering water and accomplishing (desires), traverses heaven and earth and the paths (of the firmament).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Let your course be without antelopes, o Maruts, also without horsesтАФ the course that one who is no charioteer drives.
Without halt, without reins as it crosses the dusky realm, it travels
through the two world-halves along its paths, heading toward
its goal. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

Both Geldner and Renou take pathy─Б╠Аas the obj. of s─Б╠Бdhan (e.g., тАЬтАж die rechten Wege nehmendтАЭ), but since the former is regularly used, with or without ├бnu, to express extent of space and since the latter can be used absolutely, I prefer my rendering.

Griffith

No team of goats shall draw your car, O Maruts, no horse no charioteer be he who drives it.
Halting not, reinless, through the air it travels, speeding alone its paths through earth and heaven.

Geldner

Ohne Antilopen, sogar ohne Rosse, mu├Я, ihr Marut, eure Fahrt sein, die kein Kutscher lenkt; ohne Anhalten, ohne Z├╝gel, die R├дume durcheilend, durch Himmel und Erde geht sie, die rechten Wege nehmend.

Grassmann

Auch ohne Hirsche, ohne Rosse, Maruts, durchf├дhrt eur Wagen, den kein Lenker treibet, Auch ohne Z├╝gel rastlos Luft durchdringend, die Welten dennoch, stracks den Weg verfolgend.

Elizarenkova

рд╣реЗ рдорд░реБрддрдГ рд╡рд╛рдЬрд╕рд╛рддреМ рд╕рдВрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдореЗ рдпрдореН рдЕрд╡рде рд░рдХреНрд╖рде рдЕрд╕реНрдп рдЬрдирд╕реНрдп рд╡рд░реНрддрд╛ рдкреНрд░реЗрд░рдХрдГ рди рдЕрд╕реНрддрд┐ ред рдЕрд╕реНрдп рддрд░реБрддрд╛ рдиреБ рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рд┐рддрд╛ рдЪ рди рдЕрд╕реНрддрд┐ ред рдЕрдз рдЕрдкрд┐ рдЪ рддреЛрдХреЗ рдкреБрддреНрд░реЗ рддрдирдпреЗ рдкреМрддреНрд░реЗ рдзрдиреЗ рд╡рд╛ рдЧреЛрд╖реБ рд╡рд╛ рдЕрдкреНрд╕реБ рд╡рд╛ рдирд┐рдорд┐рддреНрддрднреВрддреЗрд╖реБ ‘рдпрдореН рдЕрд╡рде рд╕рдГ рдкрд╛рд░реНрдпреЗ рд╕рдВрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдореЗ рджреНрдпреЛрдГ рджреАрдкреНрддрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдкрд┐ рд╡рд┐рдЬрд┐рдЧреАрд╖реЛрд░реНрд╡рд╛ рд╢рддреНрд░реЛрдГ рд╡реНрд░рдЬрдВ рдЧрд╡рд╛рдВ рд╕рдВрдШрдВ рджрд░реНрддрд╛ рджрд╛рд░рдпрд┐рддрд╛ рднрд╡рддрд┐ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThere is no propeller, no obstructer, of him, whom, Maruts, you protect in battle; he whom (you prosper) with sons, grandsons, cattle, and water, is in war the despoiler of the herds of his ardent (foes).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Despoiler of the herds: sa vrajam dart─Б p─Бrye adha dyoс╕е = sa gav─Бm saс╣Еgham d─Бrayit─Б saс╣Еgr─Бme dyoс╕е;

Dyoс╕е = vijigiс╣гor v─Б ┼Ыatroс╕е, of one desirous to overcome, or an enemy

Jamison Brereton

There exists now no one to obstruct, no one to overcome him whom you aid in the winning of prizes, o Maruts,
whom (you aid in the winning) of progeny, of cows, of descendants, of waters. He is the splitter of the (cow)pen just then at the decisive end of the day. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

In c, on the basis of VI.31.1 I would adjust the tr. to reflect the formulaic pair tok├б- t├бnaya- to тАЬprogeny and posterity, the waters, and the sunтАЭ; see also VI.25.4.

Flg. Geldner, Renou, and Klein (DGRV II.123, 194), the published translation takes p─Б╠Бrye тАж dy├│с╕е as referring to a particular, decisive time or hour of the day (Klein тАЬin the last (hour) of the dayтАЭ), but I now think it more likely that the phrase is simply a metrically driven variant of div├н (…) p─Б╠Бr i ye / p─Б╠Бr i ye div├н# тАЬon the decisive day,тАЭ a locution found quite commonly in the VIth Maс╣Зс╕Нala (VI.17.14, 23.2, 33.5, 40.5; also p─Б╠Бri ye ├бhan VI.26.1). In p─Бda-final position that expression is only appropriate to Jagat─л/dimeter cadences. Renou makes a similar suggestion in his comm, despite his tr. тАЬ├а lтАЩheured├йcisive du jour.тАЭ I would therefore slightly emend the published translation to тАЬon the decisive dayтАЭ; sense supports this change: the act described in this p─Бda is more likely to be localized to a particularly important day, not a particularly important part of the day.

On the tendency of ├бdha to occur adjacent to locatives, see Klein DGRV II.95.

( рдкрд╛. рдо. рез. рез. рез) рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдпрдерд╛ рд╡рд╛ рд▓реЛрдХреЗ рд░рд╛рдЬрдкреБрд░реБрд╖ рдЗрддреНрдпреБрдХреНрддреЗ рдХрд╕реНрдп рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдЮ рдЗрддрд┐ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬOffer to the loud-sounding, quick-moving, self-invigorating company of the Maruts, excellent (sacrificial) food; (to them) who overcome strength by strength; the earth trembles, Agni, at the adorable (Maruts).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Bring forward a brilliant chant for the singing, swift, self-strong Marut(-troop).
Those who overpower powers with power, before (those) combatants the earth trembles, o Agni. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

For the switch between singular reference to the Marut collectivity in ab and plural reference to the same group in cd, see disc. ad 3cd.

A particularly insistent etym. figure in c: s├бh─Бс╣Гsi s├бhas─Б s├бhante. The metrical irreg. of the p─Бda, with a likely rest at 5 (so Holland & van Nooten Rig Veda edition), after s├бh─Бс╣Гsi, may draw attention to it.

On the address to Agni in d, see comm. ad 10.

Griffith

Bring a bright hymn to praise the band of Maruts, the Singers, rapid, strong in native vigour,
Who conquer mighty strength with strength more mighty: earth shakes in terror at their wars, O Agni.

Geldner

Traget das ausgezeichnete Preislied der singenden, ├╝berlegenen, aus eigener Kraft starken Marutschar vor, die mit Gewalt die Gewalten bew├дltigen! Es bebt, o Agni, die Erde vor den reichen Herren.

Grassmann

Ein gl├дnzend Lied tragt vor der Schar der Maruts, der jubelnden, urkr├дftigen, der schnellen, Die die Gewalten durch Gewalt bew├дlt’gen, es beben Erd’ und Himmel vor den K├дmpfern.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe Maruts are resplendent as if iluminators of the sacrifice, (bright) as he flames of Agni; entitled are they to donation, and like heroes making (adversaries) tremble; brilliant are they from birth, and invincible.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Flaring like the dart of the ceremony [=ritual fire], stirring thirstily like tongues of fire,
chanting like boisterous heroes, the Maruts with their flashing birth are unassailable. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

The comparison of the Maruts to fires in 2a (y├й agn├бyo n├б ┼Ы├│┼Ыucann idh─Бn─Б╠Бс╕е тАЬthose who kept blazing up like fires being kindledтАЭ) returns here in the first hemistich with more contorted imagery. In the similes of both a and b the Maruts are compared not directly to fire, but to something that is a metaphor for fire: тАЬthe dart of the ceremonyтАЭ (a) and the more familiar тАЬtongues of fireтАЭ (b). The somewhat unexpected invocation of Agni in the last p─Бda of the preceding vs. (9d) prepares the way for these similes.

In d I have followed Geldner and Renou in selecting the final word, ├бdhс╣Ыс╣гt─Бс╕е тАШunassailableтАЩ, as the predicate. But given that the first 5 vss. of the hymn concern the MarutsтАЩ birth and that the 1st half of this vs. compares them to fire, I wonder if the predicate is rather bhr─Б╠Бjajjanm─Бnaс╕е тАШof flashing birthтАЩ, as von Bradke takes it: тАЬтАж…

leuchtend ist die Geburt der unwiderstehlichen Marut.тАЭ The striking phonology (тАжj тАжjj) of the cmpd certainly draws attention to it.

Griffith

Bright like the flashing flames of sacrifices, like tongues of fire impetuous in their onset,
Chanting their psalm, singing aloud, like heroes, splendid from birth, invincible, the Maruts.

Geldner

Hitzig wie der Brandpfeil des Opfers, gierig sich bewegend wie des Agni Zungen, ihr Lied singend wie die tosenden Helden, von Geburt schimmernd, unangreifbar sind die Marut.

Grassmann

Hell strahlend wie des Opfers Feuerflamme, voll Gier sich regend wie des Agni Zungen, Laut tobend gleich wie Helden, wenn sie st├╝rmen, die lichtgebornen Maruts unbezwinglich.

Elizarenkova

рддрдВ рдкреНрд░рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрдВ рд╡реГрдзрдиреНрддрдВ рд╡рд░реНрдзрдорд╛рдирдВ рднреНрд░рд╛рдЬрджреГрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рдВ рднреНрд░рд╛рдЬрдорд╛рдирдЛрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рдВ рд░реБрджреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рд╕реВрдиреБрдВ рдкреБрддреНрд░рдВ рдорд╛рд░реБрддрдВ рдорд░реБрджреНрдЧрдгрдВ рд╣рд╡рд╕рд╛ рд╕реНрддреЛрддреНрд░реЗрдг рдЖ рд╡рд┐рд╡рд╛рд╕реЗ рдкрд░рд┐рдЪрд░рд╛рдорд┐ ред рдХрд┐рдВрдЪ рджрд┐рд╡рдГ рд╕реНрддреЛрддреБрдГ рд╢реБрдЪрдпрдГ рдирд┐рд░реНрдорд▓рд╛: рдордиреАрд╖рд╛рдГ рд╕реНрддреБрддрдпрдГ рдЙрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдГ рдЙрджреНрдЧреВрд░реНрдгрд╛: рд╢рд░реНрдзрд╛рдп рдорд╛рд░реБрддрд╛рдп рдмрд▓рд╛рдп ред рддреГрдХреНрд╖рдГ рд╢рд░реНрдзрдГ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдмрд▓рдирд╛рдорд╕реБ рдкрд╛рдард╛рддреН ред рдЖрдкрдГ рдЖрдкреНрдиреБрд╡рдиреНрддрдГ рдЧрд┐рд░рдпреЛ рди рдореЗрдШрд╛ рдЗрд╡ ред тАШ рдЧрд┐рд░рд┐рдГ рд╡реНрд░рдЬрдГ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдореЗрдШрдирд╛рдорд╕реБ рдкрд╛рдард╛рддреН ред рдЕрд╕реНрдкреГрдзрдиреН рдЕрд╕реНрдкрд░реНрдзрдиреНрдд рее рее рео рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI worship with oblations that exalted company of the Maruts, the progeny of Rudra, armed with shining lances; the pure and earnest praises of the devout (adorer) are emulous in the invigoration (of the Maruts), as the clouds (vie in the emission of the rain).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The pure and earnest praises: divaс╕е ┼Ыardh─Бya ┼Ыucayo maniс╣г─Б girayo n─Бpa ugr─Б aspс╣Ыdhran = of heaven of the strength pure praises mountains like waters fierce have vied;

Divaс╕е = stotuс╕е, of the praiser or worshipper;

┼Ъardh─Бya = m─Бrut─Бya, for the strength of the Maruts;

Giri = megha, a cloud

Jamison Brereton

This Marut(-troop) grown strong, with flashing spears, the son(s) of Rudra I seek to entice here with an invocation.
For (the favor of) the troop of heaven the gleaming inspired thoughts, mighty like mountains or waters, have contended (with each other). с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

Note the fairly common bhr─Б╠Бjad-с╣Ыс╣гti- in a immediately following the identically formed hapax bhr─Б╠Бjaj-janman- in 10d.

The final p─Бda has attracted more concerned comment than I think it deserves; see esp. the great fuss Oldenberg makes about it. The issue is what to do with the simile containing two nominatives gir├бyo n─Б╠Бpaс╕е (= n├б ─Б╠Бpaс╕е), lit. тАЬlike mountains, waters.тАЭ The consensus seems to be that the two noms. convey a single image, with a more complex structure underlying it: namely the waters (of) the mountains, mountain water, Bergwasser. I donтАЩt see why this is necessary; instead I think the thoughts are being compared both with moutains and with waters, which are both ugr├б- in different ways. (Oldenberg allows this possibility.) Note that the adjectives qualifying the inspired thoughts, ┼Ы├║ci- and ugr├б-, were used of the Maruts earlier in the hymn, in 4c and 5c, 6a respectively.

Griffith

That swelling band I call with invocation, the brood of Rudra, armed with glittering lances.
Pure hymns are meet for that celestial army: like floods and mountains have the Strong Ones battled.

Geldner

Diese erstarkende Marutschar mit schimmernden Speeren, des Rudra S├╢hneschar bitte ich mit Anruf her. Um des Himmels Heerschar haben die lauteren Dichterworte wie die gewaltigen Bergwasser einen Wettlauf unternommen.

Grassmann

Die Marutschar, mit Lanzen funkelnd, wachsend, des Rudra Volk lock’ ich herbei durch Anruf; Der Schar des Himmels streben zu die reinen Ges├дnge, wie von Bergen m├дcht’ge Wasser.

Elizarenkova

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рдпреЗ рд╢реБрдЪрдпреЛ рдордиреАрд╖рд╛ рдЙрдЧреНрд░рд╛ рдЧрд┐рд░рдп рдЖрдкреЛ рди рджрд┐рд╡рдГ рд╢рд░реНрдзрд╛рдпрд╛рд╕реНрдкреГрдзреНрд░рдВрд╕реНрддреИрд╕реНрд╕рд╣ рд╡реГрдзрдиреНрддрдВ рдорд╛рд░реБрддрдВ рднреНрд░рд╛рдЬрджреГрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рдВ рд░реБрджреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рддрдВ рд╕реВрдиреБрдВ рд╣рд╡рд╕рд╛рд╜рд╣рдорд╛ рд╡рд┐рд╡рд╛рд╕реЗ реерезрезрее

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рддрдореН) (рд╡реГрдзрдиреНрддрдореН) рд╡рд░реНрдзрдорд╛рдирдВ рд╡рд░реНрдзрдпрдиреНрддрдВ рд╡рд╛ (рдорд╛рд░реБрддрдореН) рдорд░реБрддрд╛рдорд┐рдордореН (рднреНрд░рд╛рдЬрджреГрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рдореН) рднреНрд░рд╛рдЬрджреН рдЛрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рдГ рд╕рдореНрдкреНрд░реЗрдХреНрд╖рдгрдВ рдпрд╕реНрдп рддрдореН (рд░реБрджреНрд░рд╕реНрдп) рдХреГрддрдЪрддреБрд╢реНрдЪрддреНрд╡рд╛рд░рд┐рдВрд╢рджреНрд╡рд░реНрд╖рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордЪрд░реНрдпреНрдпрд╕реНрдп (рд╕реВрдиреБрдореН) рдкреБрддреНрд░рдореН (рд╣рд╡рд╕рд╛) рдЖрджрд╛рдиреЗрди (рдЖ) (рд╡рд┐рд╡рд╛рд╕реЗ) рд╕реЗрд╡реЗ (рджрд┐рд╡рдГ) рдХрдордиреАрдпрд╕реНрдп (рд╢рд░реНрдзрд╛рдп) рдмрд▓рд╛рдп (рд╢реБрдЪрдпрдГ) рдкрд╡рд┐рддреНрд░рд╛рдГ (рдордиреАрд╖рд╛рдГ) рдордирд╕реНрд╡рд┐рдирдГ (рдЧрд┐рд░рдпрдГ) рдореЗрдШрд╛рдГ (рди) рдЗрд╡ (рдЖрдкрдГ) рдЬрд▓рд╛рдирд┐ (рдЙрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдГ) рддреЗрдЬрд╕реНрд╡рд┐рдирдГ (рдЕрд╕реНрдкреГрдзреНрд░рдиреН) рд╕реНрдкрд░реНрджреНрдзрдиреНрддрд╛рдореН реерезрезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЕрддреНрд░реЛрдкрдорд╛рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░реМред рдпреЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛ рдореЗрдШрд╡рджреБрдиреНрдирддрд╛рдГ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдкрд╛рд▓рдХрд╛ рдЬрд▓рд╡рддреНрдкреЛрд╖рдХрд╛рдГ рдкрд╡рд┐рддреНрд░рд╛рд╢рдпрд╛рд╕реНрддреЗрдЬрд╕реНрд╡рд┐рдирдГ рдХрдордиреАрдпрд╕реНрдп рдмрд▓рд╕реНрдп рд╡рд░реНрдзрдХрд╛рдГ рд╕реНрдпреБрд╕реНрддреИрд╕реНрд╕рд╣ рдпрджрд┐ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдпрд╢рд╛рд╕рдирдВ рдХреБрд░реНрдпрд╛рддреНрддрд░реНрд╣рд┐ рдХреБрддреНрд░рд╛рдкрд┐ рдкрд░рд╛рдЬрдпреЛрд╜рдкрдХреАрд░реНрддреНрддрд┐рд╢реНрдЪ рди рдЬрд╛рдпреЗрддреЗрддрд┐ реерезрезрее рдЕрддреНрд░ рдорд░реБрджреНрдЧреБрдгрд╡рджреНрд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреНрд╡реАрд░рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ рее рдЗрддрд┐ рд╖рдЯреНрд╖рд╖реНрдЯрд┐рддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдорд╖реНрдЯрдореЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдпрд╛ рдордВрддреНрд░рд╛рдд рдЙрдкрдорд╛ рд╡ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдВрдХрд╛рд░ рдЖрд╣реЗрдд. рдЬреА рдорд╛рдгрд╕реЗ рдореЗрдШрд╛рдЪреА рд╡реГрджреНрдзреА рдХрд░рдгрд╛рд░реА, рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдкрд╛рд▓рди рдХрд░рдгрд╛рд░реА, рдЬрд▓рд╛рдкреНрд░рдорд╛рдгреЗ рдкреБрд╖реНрдЯ рдХрд░рдгрд╛рд░реА, рдкрд╡рд┐рддреНрд░ рдЖрд╢рдпрдпреБрдХреНрдд, рддреЗрдЬрд╕реНрд╡реА, рд╕реБрдВрджрд░, рдмрд▓ рд╡рд╛рдврд╡рд┐рдгрд╛рд░реА рдЕрд╕рддрд╛рдд рддреНрдпрд╛рдВрдЪреНрдпрд╛рдмрд░реЛрдмрд░ рдЬрд░ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛рдиреЗ рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдп рд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рдг рдШреЗрддрд▓реЗ рддрд░ рдХреБрдареЗрд╣реА рдкрд░рд╛рдЬрдп, рдЕрдкрдХреАрд░реНрддреА рд╣реЛрдгрд╛рд░ рдирд╛рд╣реА. рее резрез рее
